ADDIN EN.CITE.DATA [42]. Briefly, after feature scaling and PCA, a k-nearest-neighbor graph was constructed among samples, and pairwise similarities were defined by a Gaussian kernel:
where xiand xjdenote the low-dimensional representations of samples iand j, respectively. The kernel matrix was row-normalized to obtain the Markov transition matrix:
Diffusion map embedding was obtained via eigendecomposition of the transition matrix:
The root was defined as the medoid sample within the S00group in diffusion space:
The diffusion distance between samples iand jwas defined as:
Pseudotime for each sample iwas defined as the diffusion distance from the root.
Trajectory-associated features were identified using Spearman correlation with pseudotime. Global trajectory features were evaluated across all four states using the filtered matrix, whereas branch-specific trajectory features were evaluated using the full batch-corrected matrix for the S00-S10-S11 and S00-S01-S11 branches. Candidate branch features were restricted to the intersections of adjacent pairwise differential features for each branch, and significant trajectory features were defined after Benjamini-Hochberg correction. Functional enrichment analysis was performed separately for LM- and VI-associated trajectory signatures. Gene features were analyzed using clusterProfiler, whereas region-based features (OCR, peak, and window) were converted to genomic intervals and analyzed using rGREAT for ALL GO terms. Significant terms were retained using predefined adjusted significance thresholds (qvalue<0.1 or p.adjust<0.1) and integrated across feature modalities for downstream comparison and visualization.
Model construction and hyperparameter optimization
For PDAC detection, models were trained separately for each feature modality using datatype-specific input matrix generated in the preprocessing and differential-analysis steps. For count-based feature classes, including gene, FSD, peak, window, and OCR, the input matrix was obtained by variance-stabilizing transformation of the corresponding raw count matrix using PyDESeq2. For end motif and ARTEMIS, 4-mer proportion matrix and log1p transformed matrix were used as input. Hyperparameter optimization was performed within each outer training set using Optuna, to address class imbalance, SMOTE oversampling was applied within the training pipeline. Feature selection was also modality specific: artemis features were directly filtered by HSICLasso, motif features were filtered by mutual information ranking, and the remaining feature classes were first reduced by mutual information filtering and then refined by HSICLasso. The number of selected features was optimized during inner-loop tuning, and the best-performing pipeline in each outer fold was retained for evaluation.
For stage prediction, models were trained on the same datatype-specific matrices as mentioned before. Stage III and IV samples were merged into a single III/IV category, and stage labels were encoded as a multiclass outcome. Within each outer training set, Optuna was used to optimize both the number of PCA components and the feature-selection strategy. HSICLasso was applied when the number of input features exceeded the predefined threshold; otherwise, the original feature set was retained. The optimized pipeline therefore consisted of feature selection, PCA, and classifier fitting, and performance was summarized across outer folds.
For subtype modeling, regression-based progression models were constructed using the subtyping matrices and sample-level pseudotime values inferred from the trajectory analysis. Only four feature modalities (gene, peak, window, and OCR) were used. Samples were collapsed into three ordered states (S00 = 0, S10/S01 = 1, and S11 = 2) for ranking-based supervision, while continuous pseudotime values served as regression targets. Within each outer training set, features were first reduced to the top 4,000 variables ranked by mutual information with the three-level stage label. Optuna optimized the number of HSICLasso-selected features, network architecture, learning rate, and early stopping rounds. The prediction model was a fully connected neural network trained with a composite loss combining Pearson correlation loss and logistic ranking loss, with equal weights assigned to the two components. The ranking term enforced the order S00 < S10/S01 < S11, enabling the learned progression score to jointly capture continuous pseudotime structure and ordinal subtype progression.
